< Review>
History: Initially I was looking for SMOG after moving to the area and stumbled on  Folsom Care Care Center last year.  Just a basic smog inspection made me realize that there are still honest and hardworking repair faculties out there except for dealer. Amir (the owner)  made me feel at home and attended to my car in very professional manner while I sat down and sip hot coffee in a Starbucks like environment (the waiting area). The coffee, TV with news and the cleanliness was so great that I decided to use them as all my car needs going forward.

Recent experience: Yesterday I called Amir again since my dashboard was giving me suggested maintenance light for brake and cabin air filter.  I was attended with great dignity, respect and was accommodated same day for the service. Not only I saved money by not going to the dealer, I left with a very good feeling after the service since the car drove better after newly flushed brake fluid and smell great since I never replaced the cabin air filter and after the fires the car smelled like fire zone inside.

I am very particular about my cars. Even though they are old, I try to take care of them and am glad to find dealer alternative right here in Folsom.

Try them and you will not regret. I can't promise they will fix all your car issues, but I can certainly say that you will get an honest, straightforward answer to your car problems.

I am glad that I found Folsom Car Care Center and above all I made new friends. The owners, Amir & Samina, are great people and you can't go wrong with exceptional service to go on top of it.</Review>

< Text>
Finding a good vehicle repair place is always a struggle.  After years of going to a place in Orangevale because they were a family friend we just weren't happy anymore for lots of reasons.

A really good friend of mine recommended Folsom Car Care (FCC).  This friend is a DIY guy when it comes to fixing cars.  So someone who really knows cars and repairs giving us a recommendation to FCC was a real endorsement to me.

My first experience with FCC came last year after my sons car lost its  AC.  He was a week away from leaving for college out of state.  We took it to a "specialty"  AC repair shop and got a quote for just over $2,000.  We took it FCC and they repaired it quickly because of our time frame for less than a quarter of the "specialty" quote.  It has been more than 12 months and the AC still works great.  The fix was a simple pressure valve in the system that was slowly leaking down and a few other parts and a AC service that needed attention due to the age of the 2005 car.

Just recently my other sons truck needed a few Chevy service bulletins completed and general maintenance.  The truck is key to his job that pays him well for a high school kid.  We took it in on Monday for all of the repairs and got it back less than a day later with everything perfect.  He was able to start work again Wednesday morning.

I don't know everybody that works there but Jaime and Eli have both worked on my vehicles and they have come back with great work.  I am sure the rest of the team there is equally up to the task.

In the last year we have been there for:
-Navigator AC repair
-Suburban 90K maintenance
-Passat oil change
-Suburban oil change (we put a lot of miles on this vehicle)
-Chevy service bulletins and general maintenance

FCC is a quality shop with integrity and fair prices.  I highly recommend them for all your auto servicing and repair needs.

Part Two...
August 17 2020

My son was using his truck for work.  He called and told me the check engine light was flashing while he was on the freeway and when he got off the engine was running rough at idle and low speeds..  The truck has run great since it was in there in early July.  I told him to limp it home and we will deal with it in Monday.  I did some research and figured with the symptoms It is was probably a misfiring cylinder.  I have done plug and coil replacements before and I hate them. Invariably there is at least one plug that is in a bad spot to get it out and back in.  The 2004 Silverado falls into that category. I took it in told them what I thought and waited for the call saying we needed new coils and plugs.  A little more than an hour later I got  a text saying the truck was ready for pick up.  I asked what the issue was and was told it was just a loose wire to the cylinder.  During COVID when businesses are struggling to make ends meet and reman open Folsom Car Care is a great example of doing the right thing.  They could have easily called and said it needs new plugs and coils for $400-600 I would imagine.  But they took care of it for me without doing an unnecessary repair.  Thanks again guys...<//Text>

<rate>2<//rate>< review>
My daughter lives in Folsom and we were visiting her family when we got a strong coolant smell in our 2000 Ford Expedition, but only when we accelerated fairly strongly (which we only do when traffic requires it).  My son-in-law had taken his car to this outfit for some routine maintenance and seemed satisfied so I thought I would give them a try.

First of all they spent almost a full day before even looking at the problem then after another full day they said they had pressure tested the cooling system and found the leak in the upper radiator hose and recommended strongly that I also replace the lower hose and the thermostat (because all were original to the car).  I agreed and they changed me $430 for this work.  Of course, once I returned home, I had occasion to accelerate again and, guess what, the issue was not fixed at all.  I took it to another shop at here and after a prompt pressure test they told (and showed me) that the issue was a leaking heater core which ended up dripping coolant into the passenger compartment (hence the strong smell inside).

On the basis of my experience, I cannot recommend this shop and would encourage you to look elsewhere for your car care needs (perhaps excepting routing maintenance items).</review>

< Text>
This is a place that specializes in boba! I go here or get it Door Dashed whenever I can. They have a pretty large selection and readily offer milk substitutes. They carry milk teas, smoothies, lattes, teas, taiyaki (depending if the machine is warmed up or not, an order of this may take up to 10 minutes to make), slushies, waffles, and a selection of Marrianne's ice cream. They also have a few Korean style snacks. My favorites include taro milk tea with boba (boba is 50 cents extra), Earl Grey milk tea and rose garden milk tea. They also offer several toppings like flavored popping boba, mochi, clear boba, and a couple others. Customer service has always been excellent and quick.<//Text>

<Rating>5<//Rating><Text>Delicious desserts!
Drinks are fresh and sweet - but not too sweet. The secret is in the tea, I think. It's brewed just right and doesn't taste like the bagged stuff you can get from the supermarket.
As for the tapioca boba, it's just the right level of chewy and savory. And the egg waffles are crispy on the outside, while still fluffy on the inside.
I love stopping by whenever I have a craving for something sweet or refreshing.
My favorites: oolong black tea with boba when I want something cooling but not too sweet OR passion fruit green tea when I want something sweet and tart (they don't use syrup, they use passion fruit preserves so it tastes actual like passion fruit).</Text>< Pics>

<Rating>5< /Rating><text>Delicious desserts!
Drinks are fresh and sweet - but not too sweet. The secret is in the tea, I think. It's brewed just right and doesn't taste like the bagged stuff you can get from the supermarket.
As for the tapioca boba, it's just the right level of chewy and savory. And the egg waffles are crispy on the outside, while still fluffy on the inside.
I love stopping by whenever I have a craving for something sweet or refreshing.

This is a really cool little neighborhood guitar shop. Not a lot in the way of custom or boutique level gear, but most everything you'd need as a working player or hobbyist.

I'm not sure about how their prices stack up, but we live in a world of MAP policies and internet prices. That just means everyone has the same price (for the most part). The cable I bought was a fair price, and GC didn't have the inexpensive version in stock like they did.

<Review>Came in for dinner about 6:00, assuming the food would  be fresh and hot at that time.  It was neither. I've read lots of reviews of this restaurant and it seems that it has more sentimental value than food quality. Many people comment that they had been coming for years and the place is as good as it gets. It's not! Perhaps these people should investigate the Chinese buffet at ninth and Broadway in Oakland, only a mile away. Or one on International Blvd or on Willow Pass in Concord. They are four times as large, much greater selection, includes free soft drinks and a 10% senior discount. The price is only two dollars more than they Genghis Khan, a much better value.

To be more specific, I found that their sushi to be excellent and the proper was Sasabi and pickled ginger was available.  Nothing on the rest of the buffet compared favorably. The wonton soup was mildly flavorful but the wonton skins were mushy as they had  seem to have been cooked over and over. At 6 o'clock, the beginning of the dinner hour, most of the food on the buffet was only room temperature. It advertises a" seafood buffet", yet the only fish was a single flat overcooked and very unappealing filet of fish with the skin on. The mussels and clams were flavorless. The oysters while large and in the shell were not raw, as is common on other Chinese buffets, but had a dense and strange texture. When I inquired I was told that indeed they were not fresh but had been steamed. They were not served with any sauce. Steamed oysters? They were dreadful. I was disappointed. And the shrimp served in the fried shell was shriveled and tasteless. There were no tempting vegetables at all, simply a pan of chopped bell pepper and celery with a few tiny cooked shrimp thrown in, again totally tasteless. The only 'appetizer' was egg rolls, cold and greasy.

As for condiments, I've never been to a Chinese restaurant or buffet where the condiments were not available on the individual tables. These were not and one had to dish them up in small plates and carry each to the table individually. What shocked me was a large bottle of Heinz ketchup on the condiment tray by the end of the buffet table. Ketchup in a Chinese restaurant??? I should have been forewarned when I came in and saw all the tables laid out only with knife and fork, no chopstick options. I guess people in Alameda prefer this rather bland and unpleasant preparation of food as there was not an Asian in the restaurant. They were all over in Oakland's Chinatown where the food is infinitely better.

On the plus side, I will say that the atmosphere was clean, cheery, pleasant, and the waitress was very attentive in clearing dishes and bringing fresh ice water.</Review>< username>
Jeanine Fetterly<//username>

None< /pictures>

<username>David McCall< /username><Text>Can't beat it for the price.  I come in here for lunch. While the buffet food is not exquisite quality, when fresh it's as good as any asain buffet. What separates this place is the Mongolian bbq area. Since it's made to order it's always hot off the grill when it arrives to your table.  You get to decide what goes in and how to season it. It makes me laugh reading other reviews that state it (the Mongolian portion of service) lacks flavor.... guess those folks are not articulate in the culinary field...add more flavor (curry, ginger, garlic, satay, oyster, teriyaki, sweet n sour, soy sauce, Sriracha) if it lacks flavor! You are in control.</Text>< gmapID>

<Time>1616384952592<//Time><Rate>5</Rate>< Review>
This place is delicious I love Peruvian food. What I love about this place is that they have take out,recently they've added dine- in, and they have a patio for those who like to dine-out. When I went inside they have a station for sanitation, including but not limited to sanitizer, disinfectant spray, and they were wearing gloves and masks! I love the fact that so Inca is following the CDC guidelines because honestly these are the restaurants and businesses that are going to go ahead and survive especially during this pandemic. I ordered the Peruvian jalea, which is a mixture of seafood if you like the deep fried tempura pablo, breaded style seafood. What I love most about it is that it's a well served plate . Today my wife and I shared this plate and it was delicious because the price, the generous portion of the food,and the flavor is to die for. Now, just so you know they're not giving you the bread that they normally would if you dine in, but again with the seafood alone and the plate itself it's more than enough to hit the spot!<//Review>

<Name>Tim Jones< /Name><rate>5</rate>< Review>
Sol Inca is a Peruvian restaurant that has become a staple of the surrounding La Mirada community.  It has seen some name changes and change of personnel through the years.  Their place is clean and tidy.  Because it was originally a different restaurant sometimes the seating can be a little cramped.  I have been to a lot of Peruvian restaurants this by far for the quality of the food is extra ordinary.  I have not had a bad experience here.  My recommendation would be the chaufa de pollo or the lomo Saltado.  Seafood is always a specialty their but I have not experienced their wares in regards to seafood but I can only imagine with their quality in their other dishes that it will be outstanding.  You will have an enjoyable experience I just wish they would open the dance floor for a little Cumbria or salsa dancing.  Their bar is well stocked and is new.  Enjoy</Review>

<UserId.>118077039593262867913<//UserId.>< Text>
My family and I went Sol Inka to celebrate my Abuela‚Äôs 78th birthday. We are Peruvian and very familiar with Peruvian restaurants throughout Los Angeles, Sol Inka did not disappoint!

Our table ordered a variety of dishes including Lompoc Saltado, tallarin verde con bistec, ceviche and Milanesa de pollo. To be honest, everything was delicious but I really want to comment specifically on the tallarin verde. If you‚Äôve been to other Peruvian restaurants you may notice that some kitchens will dilute the sauce with spinach instead of using mostly basil (may be because of cost?). Sol Inka‚Äôs tallarin verde could easily match what my Abuela makes in her very own kitchen - don‚Äôt tell her I said that. This is a simple dish, but easy to get wrong. Sol Inka did it right, my tallarin was flavorful and zesty. The steak (bistec) was moist and cooked perfectly.

My Abuela really enjoyed her birthday here, I will definitely be back and hopefully can bring some friends next time to introduce them to Peruvian food done right!<//Text>

<date>1479748081771</date><rating>5< /rating>< Review>
I love the food here and the servers are really nice. Food can take a while, especially the soups as they are cooked to order. Portions are very large. The Lomo Saltado is a staple and is pretty speedily made, but I also like the Chicharron de Pollo as it is completely different with its bright lemony dipping sauce. Just be warned there are a lot of bones so you have to be careful when eating it.

For appetizers the calamari was really good and we like to order a side salad as it helps balance out the very carb heavy rice/fries that comes with the saltado plates.

Also soup bowls are huge.<//Review>

<UserId.>107136176059594037309<//UserId.>< username>
Luis P.</username>
<Date>1448235417294< /Date><rate>2</rate>< Text>
You go to a new place to eat, and as far as I am concerned, any dish they put in front of you, actually any edible items, is on kind of a trial. Specially if said place is heavily favorably endorsed, by over 700 reviews. Also cleanliness plays a critical part, for who would want to take a chance in a place that was plagued by unkempt hands. Not saying this about Mario's Peruvian Restaurant, just in general, for hard earned cash regrets being spent on less than reliable, tasty places. Loving with a passion authentic delicious Peruvian cuisine, I decided to stop at Mario's Peruvian Restaurant for the first time.
Let's start by calling Mario's Peruvian restaurant what it is: a sad disappointment in that they call themselves Peruvian, but they do not deliver the quality of food Peru is well known for around the world. Case in point: Choros a la Criolla, $10+ for 6 medium size mussels. The size of these tasty mollusks was certainly not the issue, it was the blunder that arrived to my table. Please allow me to explain: Choros (mussels) are served with a very fresh combination of very fine diced tomatoes, onions (preferably red onions, but not limited), chillies, sparse amount of delicious cilantro, salt, pepper, plus In some parts they add freshly boiled al dente kernels of corn, mixed altogether in a similar, but not quite, as a Pico de Gallo (The delicious Mexican version of fresh salsa), and generally the delicious Peruvian chilies that are unique to Peru (ROCOTO) add a dimension of heat to the mix well worth applauding, but of course milder options are equally tasty. The Mussels are served in the half shell, the salsa described topping each one, and on the side pieces of lemon (limes in the US, as they are comparable in acidity), and people squeezes a few drops of lemon juice to their preference.
What arrived in front of me was a semi frozen mediocre Salsa, smeared to the point of no return with lime juice or something very similar (a cardinal culinary sin, which any Peruvian cook worth their mettle would never commit), for this much lime in an old semi frozen salsa indicated it is not made daily, and for the first time in a long time I sent this overpriced dish back. 1 Star.
Ceviche Mixto, $14, with pieces of mushy fish and other seafood cooked in a citrus based sauce that did not did it any favors, slightly better than the rejected mussel dish. 3 Stars.
Bread, a little passed its prime. Green Peruvian sauce at the table, hot and tasty, made it easy to overcome the warm stale bread. Service no complaints and waiter was properly rewarded for his efforts. Water, acceptable. Lady at the front a revelation of good manners and fine figure. Time was around 12PM on a Friday.
For a place heavily endorsed by many, it did not, by any stretch of the imagination, deserve such glowing accolades, regardless if every other dish in the menu was better, which stands to doubt. 2 Stars.< /Text>
